Also note that only one instance of a particular\\n39: /// type is ever created.  Thus seeing if two types are equal is a matter of\\n40: /// doing a trivial pointer comparison. To enforce that no two equal instances\\n41: /// are created, Type instances can only be created via static factory methods\\n42: /// in class Type and in derived classes. Based on this\\n49:   /// value, you can cast to a class defined in DerivedTypes.h.\\n50:   /// Note: If you add an element to this, you need to add an element to the\\n51:   /// Type::getPrimitiveType function, or else things will break!\\n52:   /// Also update LLVMTypeKind and LLVMGetTypeKind () in the C binding.\\n53:   ///\\n54:   enum TypeID {\\n55:     // PrimitiveTypes\\n56:     HalfTyID = 0,  ///< 16-bit floating point type\\n57:     BFloatTyID,    ///< 16-bit floating point type (7-bit significand)\\n58:     FloatTyID,     ///< 32-bit floating point type\\n59:     DoubleTyID,    ///< 64-bit floating point type\\n60:     X86_FP80TyID,  ///< 80-bit floating point type (X87)\\n61:     FP128TyID,     ///< 128-bit floating point type (112-bit significand)\\n62:     PPC_FP128TyID, ///< 128-bit floating point type (two 64-bits, PowerPC)\\n63:     VoidTyID,      ///< type with no size\\n64:     LabelTyID,     ///< Labels\\n65:     MetadataTyID,  ///< Metadata\\n66:     X86_AMXTyID,   ///< AMX vectors (8192 bits, X86 specific)\\n67:     TokenTyID,     ///< Tokens\\n68: \\n69:     // Derived types... see DerivedTypes.h file.\\n70:     IntegerTyID,        ///< Arbitrary bit width integers\\n71:     FunctionTyID,       ///< Functions\\n72:     PointerTyID,        ///< Pointers\\n73:     StructTyID,         ///< Structures\\n74:     ArrayTyID,          ///< Arrays\\n75:     FixedVectorTyID,    ///< Fixed width SIMD vector type\\n76:     ScalableVectorTyID, ///< Scalable SIMD vector type\\n77:     TypedPointerTyID,   ///< Typed pointer used by some GPU targets\\n78:     TargetExtTyID,      ///< Target extension type\\n79:   };\\n80: \\n81: private:\\n82:   /// This refers to the LLVMContext in which this type was uniqued.\\n83:   LLVMContext &Context;\\n84: \\n85:   TypeID   ID : 8; Also note that only one instance of a particular\n39: /// type is ever created.  Thus seeing if two types are equal is a matter of\n40: /// doing a trivial pointer comparison. To enforce that no two equal instances\n41: /// are created, Type instances can only be created via static factory methods\n42: /// in class Type and in derived classes.  Once allocated, Types are never\n43: /// free'd.\n44: ///\n45: class Type {\n46: public:\n47:   //===--------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n48:   /// Definitions of all of the base types for the Type system.  Based on this\n49:   /// value, you can cast to a class defined in DerivedTypes.h.\n50:   /// Note: If you add an element to this, you need to add an element to the\n51:   /// Type::getPrimitiveType function, or else things will break!\n52:   /// Also update LLVMTypeKind and LLVMGetTypeKind () in the C binding.\n53:   ///\n54:   enum TypeID {\n55:     // PrimitiveTypes\n56:     HalfTyID = 0,  ///< 16-bit floating point type\n57:     BFloatTyID,    ///< 16-bit floating point type (7-bit significand)\n58:     FloatTyID,     ///< 32-bit floating point type\n59:     DoubleTyID,    ///< 64-bit floating point type\n60:     X86_FP80TyID,  ///< 80-bit floating point type (X87)\n61:     FP128TyID,     ///< 128-bit floating point type (112-bit significand)\n62:     PPC_FP128TyID, ///< 128-bit floating point type (two 64-bits, PowerPC)\n63:     VoidTyID,      ///< type with no size\n64:     LabelTyID,     ///< Labels\n65:     MetadataTyID,  ///< Metadata\n66:     X86_AMXTyID,   ///< AMX vectors (8192 bits, X86 specific)\n67:     TokenTyID,     ///< Tokens\n68: \n69:     // Derived types... see DerivedTypes.h file.\n70:     IntegerTyID,        ///< Arbitrary bit width integers\n71:     FunctionTyID,       ///< Functions\n72:     PointerTyID,        ///< Pointers\n73:     StructTyID,         ///< Structures\n74:     ArrayTyID,          ///< Arrays\n75:     FixedVectorTyID,    ///< Fixed width SIMD vector type\n76:     ScalableVectorTyID, ///< Scalable SIMD vector type\n77:     TypedPointerTyID,   ///< Typed pointer used by some GPU targets\n78:     TargetExtTyID,      ///< Target extension type\n79:   };\n80: \n81: private:\n82:   /// This refers to the LLVMContext in which this type was uniqued.\n83:   LLVMContext &Context;\n84: \n85:   TypeID   ID : 8;            // The current base type of this type.\n86:   unsigned SubclassData : 24; // Space for subclasses to store data.\n87:                               // Note that this should be synchronized with\n88:                               // MAX_INT_BITS value in IntegerType class.\n89: \n90: protected:\n91:   friend class LLVMContextImpl;\n92: \n93:   explicit Type(LLVMContext &C, TypeID tid)\n94:     : Context(C), ID(tid), SubclassData(0) {}\n95:   ~Type() = default;\n96: \n97:   unsigned getSubclassData() const { return SubclassData; \"llvm/lib/CodeGen/LowLevelTypeUtils.cpp\", \"symbol\": \"getLLTForType\"}\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"The LLVM IR type system flows from abstract type definitions through context-owned storage to machine type representations used in code generation.\\n\\n## 1. Type Class Hierarchy\\n\\nThe base `Type` class is declared in `llvm/include/llvm/IR/Type.h`. It holds a reference to the owning `LLVMContext` and defines the `TypeID` enum (IntegerTyID, FunctionTyID, StructTyID, PointerTyID, etc.). Types are immutable singletons—once created, they are never freed.\\n\\nDerived types are declared in `llvm/include/llvm/IR/DerivedTypes.h`:\\n- `IntegerType : public Type` — arbitrary-width integer, created via `IntegerType::get(LLVMContext&, unsigned NumBits)`\\n- `FunctionType : public Type` — function signature with return type and parameter list, created via `FunctionType::get(Type*, ArrayRef<Type*>, bool isVarArg)`\\n- `StructType : public Type` — aggregate type (both anonymous/literal and named), created via `StructType::get(LLVMContext&, ArrayRef<Type*>, bool IsPacked)` or `StructType::create()`\\n\\nThe SandboxIR layer mirrors these in `llvm/include/llvm/SandboxIR/Type.h` and `llvm/lib/SandboxIR/Type.cpp`, wrapping the underlying IR types via a `Context` handle.\\n\\n## 2. Context Ownership\\n\\nAll IR types are uniqued and owned by the `LLVMContext`. The private implementation lives in `llvm/lib/IR/LLVMContextImpl.h` (`LLVMContextImpl`), which stores:\\n- `DenseMap<unsigned, IntegerType *> IntegerTypes` — keyed by bit-width\\n- `FunctionTypeSet FunctionTypes` — using `FunctionTypeKeyInfo` for structural hashing\\n- `StructTypeSet AnonStructTypes` — anonymous/literal structs using `AnonStructTypeKeyInfo`\\n- `StringMap<StructType *> NamedStructTypes` — named structs by identifier\\n\\nThe factory methods implemented in `llvm/lib/IR/Type.cpp` consult these maps to ensure type uniquing: `IntegerType::get` checks `IntegerTypes`, `FunctionType::get` checks `FunctionTypes`, and `StructType::get` checks `AnonStructTypes` (or inserts into `NamedStructTypes` for named structs).\\n\\n## 3. IR Type to Machine Type Lowering in SelectionDAG\\n\\nThe lowering chain from LLVM IR types to machine types proceeds as:\\n\\n**Step 1 — EVT (Extended Value Type):** `llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/ValueTypes.h` defines `EVT`, a union of an `MVT` (simple/native machine value type) or an extended LLVM `Type*`. `TargetLowering::getValueType(const DataLayout&, Type*, bool AllowUnknown)` in `llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/TargetLowering.h` maps an IR `Type*` to `EVT`—pointer types map to the native pointer MVT, integer/float/vector types map to corresponding MVTs.\\n\\n**Step 2 — MVT (Machine Value Type):** `llvm/include/llvm/CodeGenTypes/MachineValueType.h` defines `MVT` as an enumeration of concrete register-level types (i8, i32, f64, v4i32, etc.). `EVT::getSimpleVT()` extracts the `MVT`.\\n\\n**Step 3 — SelectionDAGBuilder:** `llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/SelectionDAGBuilder.cpp` translates each LLVM IR instruction to `SDNode`s. For each IR value it calls `TLI.getValueType(DAG.getDataLayout(), I.getType())` to obtain the `EVT` before constructing DAG nodes. Multiple EVTs may be needed per value for aggregate/multi-value types.\\n\\n**Step 4 — FunctionLoweringInfo:** `llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/FunctionLoweringInfo.cpp` pre-processes the IR function, computing value types for all IR values to guide SelectionDAG construction.\\n\\n**Step 5 — Reverse mapping:** `EVT::getTypeForEVT(LLVMContext&)` in `llvm/lib/CodeGen/ValueTypes.cpp` converts back from EVT to LLVM IR `Type*` when required.\\n\\n**Step 6 — GlobalISel LLT:** For the GlobalISel pipeline, `getLLTForType(Type&, DataLayout&)` in `llvm/lib/CodeGen/LowLevelTypeUtils.cpp` converts IR types to `LLT` (Low-Level Type), defined in `llvm/include/llvm/CodeGenTypes/LowLevelType.h`. This provides a target-independent representation used by GlobalISel instead of SelectionDAG's EVT/MVT.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
